1895-09-12 00:00:00 Scene 0 --- Participants: ['Della Plumstone', 'Lennon Figtree']
    Event statement
  • Della Plumstone -- premise: The first rays of dawn painted the sky above Fruitville in hues of orange and gold, casting a warm glow over the bustling market. Stalls overflowed with vibrant fruits, their aromas mingling in the crisp morning air. Della Plumstone is trying to buy some fruit from Lennon Figtree. They are negotiating a price. Della Plumstone can sell the fruit for 6 coins back in her home town.
    Lennon Figtree -- premise: The first rays of dawn painted the sky above Fruitville in hues of orange and gold, casting a warm glow over the bustling market. Stalls overflowed with vibrant fruits, their aromas mingling in the crisp morning air. Lennon Figtree is trying to sell some fruit. He is negotiating a price with Della Plumstone. It costs Lennon Figtree 1 coin to buy the fruit from the farm.

Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

          [28 Oct 1889 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 21 years old, she faced a particularly harsh winter that threatened to wipe out her entire stock of fruit. Undeterred, Della bundled herself in warm clothes and traveled to a neighboring village, bartering her remaining fruit for dried goods and supplies that would last her through the cold months. This experience taught her the importance of resourcefulness and adaptability in the face of adversity.

    • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master. You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

          [28 Oct 1875 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 6 years old, she experienced her first taste of independence when she was tasked with taking a basket of freshly picked strawberries to their grandmother who lived on the other side of the village. Although the journey was short, Della felt a surge of pride as she carefully navigated the dirt paths, her small hands clutching the wicker basket tight. She imagined herself a tiny merchant, delivering precious cargo.
          [28 Oct 1879 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 9 years old, a terrible hailstorm ravaged their family’s orchard, destroying most of the fruit trees. Despite the devastation, Della refused to give in to despair; instead, she helped her parents clear the debris and plant new saplings, her small hands working tirelessly alongside theirs. This experience instilled in her a deep understanding of the unpredictable nature of life and the importance of perseverance.
          [28 Oct 1882 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 13 years old, she bartered a basket of her family's apples for a worn copy of "One Thousand and One Nights." She spent hours poring over the tales of faraway lands and exotic fruits, her imagination ignited by the stories of merchants and adventurers. This sparked a longing in Della to see the world beyond her village and experience its wonders firsthand.
          [28 Oct 1885 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 16 years old, she convinced her parents to let her travel to the nearby town to sell surplus fruit from the family farm. She carefully arranged the peaches, plums, and pears in her cart, her heart pounding with a mixture of excitement and nervousness. This first foray into trading ignited a passion in Della for the art of bartering and the joy of connecting with people from different walks of life.
          [28 Oct 1887 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 19 years old, she encountered a dishonest merchant who tried to cheat her out of a fair price for her apples. Using her sharp wit and knowledge of fruit quality, Della stood her ground and negotiated a fair deal, refusing to be taken advantage of. This experience solidified her determination to be a fair and honest trader, someone who could be trusted.
          [28 Oct 1889 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 21 years old, she faced a particularly harsh winter that threatened to wipe out her entire stock of fruit. Undeterred, Della bundled herself in warm clothes and traveled to a neighboring village, bartering her remaining fruit for dried goods and supplies that would last her through the cold months. This experience taught her the importance of resourcefulness and adaptability in the face of adversity.

    • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master. You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

She imagined herself a tiny merchant, delivering precious cargo.
          [28 Oct 1879 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 9 years old, a terrible hailstorm ravaged their family’s orchard, destroying most of the fruit trees. Despite the devastation, Della refused to give in to despair; instead, she helped her parents clear the debris and plant new saplings, her small hands working tirelessly alongside theirs. This experience instilled in her a deep understanding of the unpredictable nature of life and the importance of perseverance.
          [28 Oct 1882 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 13 years old, she bartered a basket of her family's apples for a worn copy of "One Thousand and One Nights." She spent hours poring over the tales of faraway lands and exotic fruits, her imagination ignited by the stories of merchants and adventurers. This sparked a longing in Della to see the world beyond her village and experience its wonders firsthand.
          [28 Oct 1885 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 16 years old, she convinced her parents to let her travel to the nearby town to sell surplus fruit from the family farm. She carefully arranged the peaches, plums, and pears in her cart, her heart pounding with a mixture of excitement and nervousness. This first foray into trading ignited a passion in Della for the art of bartering and the joy of connecting with people from different walks of life.
          [28 Oct 1887 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 19 years old, she encountered a dishonest merchant who tried to cheat her out of a fair price for her apples. Using her sharp wit and knowledge of fruit quality, Della stood her ground and negotiated a fair deal, refusing to be taken advantage of. This experience solidified her determination to be a fair and honest trader, someone who could be trusted.
          [28 Oct 1889 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 21 years old, she faced a particularly harsh winter that threatened to wipe out her entire stock of fruit. Undeterred, Della bundled herself in warm clothes and traveled to a neighboring village, bartering her remaining fruit for dried goods and supplies that would last her through the cold months. This experience taught her the importance of resourcefulness and adaptability in the face of adversity.

    • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master. You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

    • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master. You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.
